ITEM NO.1501               COURT NO.3               SECTION XII-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Civil Appeal  No(s).  4665-4666/2025
MANIYAR ILIYAZ @ SHAIK RIYAZ & ANR.                Appellant(s)
                                VERSUS
P. AYYAPPAN & ORS.                                 Respondent(s)
[ HEARD BY : HON. PAMIDIGHANTAM SRI NARASIMHA AND HON. ATUL S. 
CHANDURKAR, JJ. ] 
 
Date : 19-06-2026 These appeals were called on for pronouncement of
   judgment today.
For Appellant(s) : Mr. Sharanagouda Patil, Adv.
                   Mrs. Supreeta Sharanagouda, Adv.
                   Ms. Supreeta Sharanagouda, AOR
                   
                   Mr. Mamidipudi Venkatarama Mukunda, A.C.
                   
For Respondent(s) :Mr. Abhisth Kumar, AOR
                   Mr. Zorawar Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. Jayant Rastogi, Adv.
                                     
1. Hon’ble Mr. Justice Pamidighantam Sri Narasimha pronounced the
judgment of the Bench comprising His Lordship and Hon’ble Mr.
Justice Atul S. Chandurkar. 
2. The appeals are disposed of in terms of the signed reportable
judgment. Paragraph nos. 19 to 22 of the Judgment read as under:-
“19. In this view of the matter, the appellant(s)
will  be  entitled  to  compensation  of  Rs.
11,44,628/- and the amount shall be paid within a
period of two months from today. 
20. Returning  to  the  discussion  and  the
articulation of the right, the correlative duty
and  followed  by  the  constitutional  statutory
remedies, in conclusion, we declare as under: 
a. The right to walk is a fundamental
right under Part III of the Constitution. It
is  integral  to  the  right  to  movement
guaranteed under Article 19(1)(d), read with

--- Page 251 ---
Article 19(1)(a), Article 19(1) (b), Article
19(1) (c) and Article 21 of the Constitution
of India. The fundamental right to walk will
take  within  its  sweep  the  right  to
demarcated  footpaths.  These  rights  are
primary  and  shall  have  priority  over
movement by motorised vehicles.
b. The  fundamental  right  to  walk  on
demarcated footpaths has a correlative duty.
If the road exists, there is a duty to
ensure that there are demarcated and well-
maintained footpaths for walkers. The duty
bearers  are  the  urban  development
authorities,  municipal  corporations,
municipalities and even panchayats, who must
endeavour to demarcate, construct, maintain,
and safeguard footpaths and other necessary
pedestrian  infrastructure,  as  walking  is
integral to life. 
c. The violation of the right to walk on
demarcated  footpaths  will  entitle  the
citizens to invoke constitutional and legal
remedies  against  duty  bearers  for
restitution and compensation. This remedy is
independent  of  the  remedies  that  are
available  under  the  Motor  Vehicles  Act,
1988.  
21. We place on record the valuable assistance
rendered by Mr. Mamidipudi V Mukunda, learned
counsel appointed as amicus curiae. We direct the
Registry to re-number this case as a petition
under Article 32 of the Constitution by changing
the cause title to Re: Fundamental Right to Walk
and Footpath . The Government of India, through
the Ministries of Housing and Urban Affairs,
Rural  Development  and  Road  Transport  and
Highways, is impleaded as a party in person. We
request Mr. K.M. Nataraj, ASG, to assist the
court.
22. The appeal(s) and pending application(s), if
any, are disposed of accordingly. No order as to
costs. ”
(KAPIL TANDON)                                  (POOJA SHARMA)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)
(Signed Reportable Judgment is placed on the file.)

--- Page 252 ---

               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS

[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  19-05-2026

Delhi]
YUGANTER & ORS.                                    Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF NCT OF DELHI & ANR.                   Respondent(s)
IA No. 175371/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED
JUDGMENT, IA No. 175369/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 19-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE UJJAL BHUYAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ARUN PALLI
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Pradeep Kumar Yadav, Adv.
                   Mr. Taiyyab Khan Salmani, Adv.
                   Mr. Deepak Yadav, Adv.
                   Ms. Prakriti Pandey, Adv.
                   Ms. Khushboo, Adv.
                   Mr. Sanjeev Malhotra, AOR
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard Mr. Pradeep Kumar Yadav, learned
counsel for the petitioner.
2. The impugned order of the High Court reads thus:
“1. Petitioners  seek  quashing  FIR
No.92/2024 of FIR No.92/2024 of PS Crime
(Women) Cell for offence under Section
498A/406/34  IPC  on  the  ground  that
complainant de facto (respondent no.2)
has  settled  the  disputes  with  the
1

--- Page 253 ---
petitioners.
2. On  being  pointed  out  extremely
serious allegations in the FIR regarding
forcible abortion, which is an offence
under Section 91 BNS, learned counsel for
the petitioners on instructions of his
clients  present  courtroom  seeks
permission to withdraw this petition so
that petitioners face trial.
3. As requested, the petition and the
accompanying application are dismissed as
withdrawn.”
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that both
husband and wife are present in Court and they are
willing to settle the matter.
4. While we appreciate the endeavor of the learned
counsel  for  the  petitioner  for  resolution  of  the
matrimonial dispute, we are however of the view that
since the petition seeking quashing of FIR was withdrawn
by  the  petitioner  on  specific  instructions  of  the
petitioner who was present in Court, it would be more
appropriate if the petitioner moves an application before
the High Court for recall of the order dated 19.05.2026
and makes submission regarding settlement of the dispute.

                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Special Leave Petition (Crl.)  No(s).  11438-11440/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 27-05-2026
passed  by  the  Hon’ble  High  Court  of  Punjab  and  Haryana  at
Chandigarh in Criminal Appeal No. CRA-D-923-2026 (O&M)]
RIZWAN                                             Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF HARYANA                                   Respondent(s)
IA No. 180751/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 180750/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 18-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) Mr. M R Shamshad, Sr. Adv.
                   Mr. Abu Bakr Sabbaq, Adv.
                   Mr. Shashank Singh, AOR
                   Mr. Arijit Sarkar, Adv.
                   Ms. Prapti Shrivastava, Adv.
                   Ms. Saiyyada, Adv.
                   Mr. Varun Singh, Adv.
                                      
For Respondent(s) : Mr. Abhinav Bajaj, AAG
Mr. Saksham Ojha, Adv.
Ms. Geetashi Chadra, Adv.
Mr. Rahul Khurana, AOR
Ms. Bhavya Singla, Adv.
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. In  view  of  the  law  declared  in  M  Ravindran  vs.  The
Intelligence Officer, Directorate of Revenue Intelligence [(2021) 2
SCC 485], we are of the opinion that the order dated 02.06.2026
extending period of detention under proviso to Section 43 (D)(2)(b)

--- Page 257 ---
2
of the Unlawful Activities (Prevention) Act, 1967 would relate back
to the date of the application for extension i.e., 19.02.2026, made
prior to the prayer for default bail dated 11.05.2026. Our view is
fortified by the well-settled principle ‘ actus curiae neminem
gravabit’ – that is an act of court cannot prejudice a party. The
failure of the Trial Court to notify the accused in the earlier
hearing could not have prejudiced the prayer of the prosecution to
seek extension, which the latter had already sought prior to the
prayer for default bail.
3. In the given circumstances, we are not inclined to interfere
with the impugned order passed by the High Court. However, in view
of the fact that investigation has concluded and final report has
been filed, petitioner would be at liberty to seek bail on merits
which shall be decided independently in accordance with law.
4. With the above observations, the Special Leave Petitions are
dismissed.
5. Pending applications, if any, shall stand disposed of.
(KANCHAN CHOUHAN)                              (CHETNA BALOONI)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)

in DBSAW No. 539/2026 27-05-2026 in DBSAW No. 544/2026 27-05-2026
in DBSAW No. 538/2026 passed by the High Court of Judicature for
Rajasthan at Jaipur]
D.B. CORP LTD. (DAINIK BHASKAR)                    Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
SANJAY GAUTAM & ORS.                               Respondent(s)
FOR ADMISSION 
IA No. 181314/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 18-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE S.V.N. BHATTI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ATUL S. CHANDURKAR
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Ms. Amrita Sarkar , AOR
                   Mr. Rahul Pandey, Adv.
                   Mr. Ashish Kumar Singh, Adv.
                    
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner.
2. The petitioner challenges the order dated 27.05.2026 and the
challenge is confined to what has been set out in paragraph number
10 of the impugned order, which reads as under:
1

--- Page 281 ---
“At this stage, learned Senior counsel appearing
for the appellants submits that the appellants may
be allowed to raise objections, we are afraid that
we cannot give such permission to the appellants as
the aspect regarding computation of the amount is
on the basis of the order, which has already been
passed allowing the application moved under Section
33(c)(2) of the Act.”
3. The learned counsel would urge that the High Court has felt the
need and necessity for the Labour Court to determine the amount
payable under Section 33(c)(2) of the Industrial Disputes Act,
1947, and the determination is never on the details permissible to
one of the parties. The petitioner has legitimate objections to the
calculations furnished by the workmen. It should be given an
ordinance.
4. We are not interfering with the substantive portion of the order
impugned. We find it unnecessary to issue notice or stop the
exercise directed by the High Court under the impugned order.
However, to meet the ends of justice and also the requirement of
Section 33(c) (2), we observe that the Labour Court furnishes a
copy of the calculation filed by the workmen and the petitioner is
given two weeks’ time to file its objections, if any. Upon receipt
of such objections, the matter is decided by the Labour Court, and
the petitioner is permitted to file a letter before the Labour
Court informing it of the order passed by this Court on the same
date.
5. With these observations, these special leave petitions stand
disposed of.
6. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of. 
(RASHI GUPTA)                                   (NIKITA SINGH)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)
2

--- Page 282 ---

                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CIVIL) DIARY NO(S). 27607/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 13-04-2023
in WP No. 4786/2015 passed by the High Court of Judicature at
Bombay]
STATE OF MAHARASHTRA & ORS.                        Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
NITIN BHAGWAN CHAVAN & ANR.                        Respondent(s)
IA No. 171521/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING
IA No. 171523/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 171524/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
IA No. 171526/2026 - PERMISSION TO FILE ADDITIONAL 
DOCUMENTS/FACTS/ANNEXURES
 
Date : 18-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SANDEEP MEHTA
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIJAY BISHNOI
    [PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Shrirang B. Varma, Adv.
                   Mr. Siddharth Dharmadhikari, Adv.
                   Mr. Aaditya Aniruddha Pande, AOR 
                  
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
This special leave petition is delayed by 1028
days.
The controversy involved in this special leave
petition  is  squarely  covered  by  the  decision
rendered  in  Maharashtra  Adiwasi  Thakur  Jamat
Swarakshan Samiti v. State of Maharashtra and Others
1

--- Page 303 ---
SLP (C) D. No. 27607 of 2026
reported in (2023) 16 SCC 415, which is relied upon
by the High Court while passing the impugned order
dated 13th April, 2023.
In spite of these glaring facts, the State
Government has preferred the instant special leave
petition with a gross and undue delay of 1028 days.
The reasons assigned in the application seeking
condonation of delay are virtually non-existent or
woefully inadequate to say the least.
We, therefore, express serious reservations on
the conduct of officials concerned of the State
Government in preferring this highly belated special
leave petition involving a controversy which stands
covered by a decision of this Court in Maharashtra
Adiwasi  Thakur  Jamat  Swarakshan  Samiti  (supra)
rendered way back on 24 th March, 2023. The officials
concerned are advised to remain careful in future.
The special leave petition is dismissed on the
ground of delay as well as on merits.
Pending application(s), if any, shall stand
disposed of.
Copy of this order shall be placed before the
Chief Secretary, Maharashtra for information.
(SHIPRA NARANG)                             (NIDHI WASON)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     ASSISTANT REGISTRAR
2

                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CIVIL)……………….. Diary No(s). 22911/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 17-03-2026
in WP No.2714/2026 passed by the High Court of Madhya Pradesh
Principal Seat at Jabalpur]
JITENDRA LILHARE                                   Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF MADHYA PRADESH & ORS.                 Respondent(s)
IA No. 169481/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN REFILING/CURING THE
DEFECTS, IA No. 169480/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE
IMPUGNED JUDGMENT, IA No. 169478/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 18-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE THE CHIEF JUSTICE
         HON'BLE MRS. JUSTICE V. MOHANA
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Varun Thakur, Adv.
                   Mr. Ramkaran, Adv.
                   Mr. Chandan Kumar Singh, Adv.
                   Mrs. Shraddha Saran, Adv.
                   Dr. M K Ravi, Adv.
                   Mr. S P Singh, Adv.
                                      
For Respondent(s) : Mr. Sridhar Potaraju, Sr. Adv. (AAG)
Mr. Harmeet Singh Ruprah, AOR
Mr. Karan Singh, Adv.
Ms. Arlene Noronha, Adv. 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. A  letter  has  been  circulated  by  the  petitioner  seeking
adjournment of two weeks in this matter. However, it is pointed out
by learned Senior Counsel for the State of Madhya Pradesh that the
petitioner is misusing the pendency of these proceedings. 
1

--- Page 309 ---
3. In support of his claims, the learned Senior Counsel for the
respondent-State has tendered screenshots of certain posts made by
the petitioner on the social-media website ‘Facebook’. From a bare
perusal of these screenshots, it is observed that the petitioner is
publicly making claims about the instant matter’s Case Status and
listing  dates.  The  petitioner  also  brazenly  appears  to  be
commenting on the kind of order(s) this Court is expected to pass. 
4. In such a view of the matter, we decline the request for
adjournment sought by the petitioner.
5. Heard Mr. Thakur, learned counsel for the petitioner and
learned Senior Counsel for the respondent-State.
6. We see no ground to interfere with the impugned judgment dated
17.03.2026 passed by the High Court of Madhya Pradesh. However, in
the peculiar facts and circumstances of this case, the impugned
order is modified to the extent of setting aside the costs imposed
upon the petitioner, i.e. Rs.1 lakh. We hasten to clarify that this
relaxation is strictly subject to the petitioner’s continued good
conduct, and we caution and warn him that the costs shall stand
revived in case he is found indulging in such frivolous litigation
in the future.
7. The Special Leave Petition is, accordingly, dismissed.
8. All pending applications, if any, also stand disposed of.
(ARJUN BISHT)                                (PREETHI DILEEP KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                         DEPUTY REGISTRAR
